  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11915880033666477">In THE OTHER SIDE OF MIDNIGHT, they played the ultimate game of love, lust, and death.<br /><br />Now, in MEMORIES OF MIDNIGHT, the survivors meet to play one last time...<br /><br />Shadowed by tragedy and burdened by amnesia, a beautiful woman desperately tries to return to reality. She is Catherine Douglas, destined to once again challenge the cruel, charismatic power of Constantin Demiris, the Greek shipping tycoon who murdered Catherine's husband. Now, in the glittering capitals and carefree playgrounds of post-war Europe, Demiris sets his deadly sights on Catherine -- and the single, treacherous secret whose shattering truth is known to her alone...</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer645011762">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7879084371718418781">What a painful read this has been!<br />Everything from the plot to the writing was utterly banal. This book didn't manage to quirk my interest at any point. The whole thing to me seemed blatantly stupid, to be honest.<br />Characters, along with being hackneyed were also completely unrealistic. Especially, Constantin Dimires who was most ludicrous of all. <br />I've read 2 Sidney Sheldon books before this and one thing that I've found to be consistent in his novels is the dreadful writing. The language, as alway</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7879084371718418781">What a painful read this has been!<br />Everything from the plot to the writing was utterly banal. This book didn't manage to quirk my interest at any point. The whole thing to me seemed blatantly stupid, to be honest.<br />Characters, along with being hackneyed were also completely unrealistic. Especially, Constantin Dimires who was most ludicrous of all. <br />I've read 2 Sidney Sheldon books before this and one thing that I've found to be consistent in his novels is the dreadful writing. The language, as always, was extremely appalling and the plot even more asinine.<br />After this book, I seem to have developed a strong aversion to Sheldon's books, for good. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_357010023">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/357010023" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5709335-jeremy-bates" class="left imgcol" title="Jeremy Bates"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1450589304p2/5709335.jpg" alt="Jeremy Bates" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/357010023?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 04, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5709335-jeremy-bates" class="user" title="Jeremy Bates">Jeremy Bates</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer357010023">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13110950434747304053"><em>Memories of Midnight</em> (1990) is a sequel to <em>The Other Side of Midnight</em> (1973), what many people consider to be one of his best novels. <em>Memories</em>, however, holds its own mixing revenge, greed, justice, and romance.<br /><br />I think it's a sign of a good book if, after some ten odd years, you can read it again and remember nearly all of the characters. That's what this one was like for me.<br /><br />Demiris, the vengeful Greek billionaire; Chotas, the brilliant lawyer; and Catherine, the amnesic who just wants to fall i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13110950434747304053"><em>Memories of Midnight</em> (1990) is a sequel to <em>The Other Side of Midnight</em> (1973), what many people consider to be one of his best novels. <em>Memories</em>, however, holds its own mixing revenge, greed, justice, and romance.<br /><br />I think it's a sign of a good book if, after some ten odd years, you can read it again and remember nearly all of the characters. That's what this one was like for me.<br /><br />Demiris, the vengeful Greek billionaire; Chotas, the brilliant lawyer; and Catherine, the amnesic who just wants to fall in love (the weakest character of the bunch, imo).<br /><br />Nevertheless, Sheldon is a master of plot. In fact I don't know anyone who writes as breezy as he does (a good thing), while throwing in as many twists and turns.<br /><br />I think part of James Patterson's success is due to his incredibly short chapters. Like them or not, it just makes you feel like you're flipping the pages faster (and you are because of all the white space!) Similarly, part of Sheldon's success I think is due not to short chapters but his short paragraphs. Anywhere he can fit in a break (#) he does. It's a good technique to keep things moving, and it allows him to jump all over the place and get inside everyone's head seemingly without effort.<br /><br />More than any of Sydney Sheldon’s novels, <em>Memories of Midnight</em> shows that the author comes from the movie and television script writing with its short scenes and generic descriptions of people and settings.<br /><br />The late Sydney Sheldon was the author of eighteen bestselling novels. He wrote more than 200 television scripts and twenty-five movie scripts and six Broadway scripts. He started writing novels at the age of fifty.<br /><br />Highly recommended.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13110950434747304053">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/19253213-heena-p" class="user" title="Heena P.">Heena P.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

              <a href="/review/list/19253213-heena-p?shelf=read-in-2014" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2014</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer950344055'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer950344055">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11594857380382500312">Memories is a brilliant novel that keeps the juices of one’s mind flowing. It’s an ultimate page-turner. I love Sidney Sheldon’s books but this one is one of his best books. No matter how old the books are, or infact how many times you read them, they really keep you engaged!<br />This book is the sequel to The Other Side Of Midnight and rotates about Catherine (Larry Douglas’s wife). At the end of the first book she lost her memory and in this book, around a year later, she starts to regain it bit by</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11594857380382500312">Memories is a brilliant novel that keeps the juices of one’s mind flowing. It’s an ultimate page-turner. I love Sidney Sheldon’s books but this one is one of his best books. No matter how old the books are, or infact how many times you read them, they really keep you engaged!<br />This book is the sequel to The Other Side Of Midnight and rotates about Catherine (Larry Douglas’s wife). At the end of the first book she lost her memory and in this book, around a year later, she starts to regain it bit by bit. This poses a threat to Constantin Demiris and he decided to take one last revenge with Larry Douglas (even though he’s dead), by sexually exploiting his wife and then killing her. He waits for the right moment for this but other loose ends, regarding Noel’s and Larry’s cold-blooded murder by Costa, starts to come up and he gets busy planning quite a few murders.<br />Some new characters are also introduced and they play a major role in the downfall of Costa. This book familiarises the reader with the life of our beloved Constantin Demiris (past and present) and how he pays for all he does.<br />Catherine meanwhile remains the main focus of the book and also the Costa’s target. After The death of Kirk Reynold’s (a co-worker whom she dates) in an skiing accident and two lawyer’s random deaths (involved in Larry’s trial) , she starts to feel that everyone around her die’s and goes in depression. Then she visits a psychiatrist named Alan, who actually plays a small part of our hero.<br />The end is predictable but the way it is written is just amazing. You’ll definitely not be able to leave the book even for a second in the last 50 pages! Atleast I wasn't able to. The end of Costa was quite unimaginable!<br />I would definitely recommend it to everyone who hasn't already read it, especially to those who love thriller and mystery.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/346444016?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 15, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas" class="user" title="Benjamin Thomas">Benjamin Thomas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=thriller" class="actionLinkLite">thriller</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer346444016">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2889660172217311261">This is the sequel to <a title="The Other Side of Midnight by Sidney Sheldon" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/136167.The_Other_Side_of_Midnight">The Other Side of Midnight</a> and a worthy sequel all round. While the first was published in 1973, it wasn't until 1990 that this sequel was published. And since the first could have easily stood alone, I feel sure the author bowed to reader and publisher demand to provide a follow-up. Often that scenario ends in disaster for the second book but that's not the case here.<br /><br />This is basically a book of double-crossing. I mean everybody double and triple crosses everybody else in t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2889660172217311261">This is the sequel to <a title="The Other Side of Midnight by Sidney Sheldon" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/136167.The_Other_Side_of_Midnight">The Other Side of Midnight</a> and a worthy sequel all round. While the first was published in 1973, it wasn't until 1990 that this sequel was published. And since the first could have easily stood alone, I feel sure the author bowed to reader and publisher demand to provide a follow-up. Often that scenario ends in disaster for the second book but that's not the case here.<br /><br />This is basically a book of double-crossing. I mean everybody double and triple crosses everybody else in this story and so the fun of reading it becomes trying to figure out just how it's going to be done. One of the main characters from the first book is back, Catherine Alexander, but unfortunately, she is the patsy for all the other characters and batted about like a ping pong ball throughout the plot. For those readers of the first book who were left unfulfilled because not all story lines were fully resolved or for those that needed to have justice for the "bad" guys, then this is a must read.<br /><br />Overall a fun book to read.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2889660172217311261">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_173029431">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173029431" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5164237-azzahro-wijaya" class="left imgcol" title="Azzahro Wijaya"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Azzahro Wijaya" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/173029431?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 02, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5164237-azzahro-wijaya" class="user" title="Azzahro Wijaya">Azzahro Wijaya</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6629866-padang-bayang-kelabu" title="Paperback 9795111566" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5164237-azzahro-wijaya?shelf=sidney-sheldon" class="actionLinkLite">sidney-sheldon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer173029431">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8464729648969483248">Saya salut sama Sidney Sheldon. Saya salut sama Constantin Demiris. Setiap kali membaca novel karya Sidney Sheldon, saya selalu "ditipu" dengan berbagai cara. di Novel ini Demiris yang tengah dipermainkan oleh rivalnya yang berusaha menjatuhkannya, bersikap seolah-olah ia akan kalah. Namun pada akhirnya ia berhasil memenangkan pertandingan sengit kepada rival-rivalnya. <br /><br />Noel Page yang berhasil dibunuhnya seakan-akan bangkit dari kubur untuk membalas dendam kepada Constantin Demiris, namun Costa t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8464729648969483248">Saya salut sama Sidney Sheldon. Saya salut sama Constantin Demiris. Setiap kali membaca novel karya Sidney Sheldon, saya selalu "ditipu" dengan berbagai cara. di Novel ini Demiris yang tengah dipermainkan oleh rivalnya yang berusaha menjatuhkannya, bersikap seolah-olah ia akan kalah. Namun pada akhirnya ia berhasil memenangkan pertandingan sengit kepada rival-rivalnya. <br /><br />Noel Page yang berhasil dibunuhnya seakan-akan bangkit dari kubur untuk membalas dendam kepada Constantin Demiris, namun Costa tetap banyak akal untuk menghancurkan siapa saja yang menghalangi jalannya. Namun pada akhirnya, ia menerima ganjaran atas apa yang telah diperbuatnya di dunia.<br /><br />Anehnya, di novel ini Sidney Sheldon mengemukakan idenya bahwa orang-orang Amerika selalu percaya pada "happy ending", dan itulah yang membuat mereka konyol. Realita tidak sama dengan apa yang diungkapkan dalam buku cerita, namun Sidney Sheldon dalam setiap novelnya seakan-akan mengatakan "yang baik akan menang<br />", "kejahatan akan menerima ganjarannya", dan "pernikahan adalah sebuah bentuk dari Happy ending yang sempurna."<br /><br />Sidney Sheldon kebanyakan bercerita tentang wanita-wanita yang hebat dan tegar, mungkin karena itulah karyanya didominasi oleh pembaca wanita. Para wanita tentunya ingin turut merasakan hebatnya berpetualang menjelajah dunia dan menjadi orang hebat yang selalu dicerminkan dalam-karya-karyanya daripada hanya diam di rumah sambil berpikir "akan masak apa kita hari ini?".</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8464729648969483248">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Trust me, you'll keep thinking throughout the entire read - "Is he the killer, is she the culprit? Is she really gonna do this?! Nah! She hasn't got the balls for that! Meh."   <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/533225168" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5265333-kimberly-hicks" class="left imgcol" title="Kimberly Hicks"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1356739073p2/5265333.jpg" alt="Kimberly Hicks" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/533225168?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 09, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5265333-kimberly-hicks" class="user" title="Kimberly Hicks">Kimberly Hicks</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/218268.Memories_of_Midnight" title="Hardcover 9780688084882" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kimberly by: </span>
      Goodreads
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5265333-kimberly-hicks?shelf=read-on-kindle" class="actionLinkLite">read-on-kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer533225168">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14536703913013763405">Well, for many years I often wondered what Memories of Midnight would be about, and after having read it, I'm happy to say, it was the perfect ending to an outstanding story.<br /><br />This novel focused on Catherine Alexander, the character we first met in The Other Side of Midnight. And you will learn more about the great Constantin Demiris. In fact, had it not been for dear old Costa, we wouldn't have had much of a novel.<br /><br />I felt Sidney did a great job summing up the characters I grew to love in the first</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14536703913013763405">Well, for many years I often wondered what Memories of Midnight would be about, and after having read it, I'm happy to say, it was the perfect ending to an outstanding story.<br /><br />This novel focused on Catherine Alexander, the character we first met in The Other Side of Midnight. And you will learn more about the great Constantin Demiris. In fact, had it not been for dear old Costa, we wouldn't have had much of a novel.<br /><br />I felt Sidney did a great job summing up the characters I grew to love in the first one. My only problem was I truly missed Noelle and Larry. Of course, if you read the first book, you know what happened to those characters, and I have to say they were sorely missed; however, if they were in this sequel, I'm not sure this book would have had the infamous twists and turns that Sidney was so well-known for doing. He was truly the master of plots. <br /><br />If you've never read one of his books, his writing sort of reminds you of a Law and Order episode, where there are several little stories that build up into a huge one. I've never read another author who can quite come up to Sidney's standard. I see why he won so many awards because he was truly a gifted author. I miss his work, but it's nice to revisit what he's left for us readers to intake.<br /><br />You will definitely enjoy this novel. Great read and fast paced!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14536703913013763405">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer841939869">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10938072074505977270">Read this book without realising that it was a sequel. This can be read as a stand alone book too.( Though i did wonder about the character of Larry; will now have to read the other side of midnight to discover that).<br /> Having said that, this book doesnot live up to the reputation of the author. While it starts off interestingly with a girl with a mysterious past, the method by which she remembers her past is not particularly interesting. (she wakes up and then happens to remember a part of her li</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10938072074505977270">Read this book without realising that it was a sequel. This can be read as a stand alone book too.( Though i did wonder about the character of Larry; will now have to read the other side of midnight to discover that).<br /> Having said that, this book doesnot live up to the reputation of the author. While it starts off interestingly with a girl with a mysterious past, the method by which she remembers her past is not particularly interesting. (she wakes up and then happens to remember a part of her life). <br />For a Sheldon heroine, the character of Catherine is quite boring (all the time wondering only if she will fall in love again) and not particularly smart either, inspite of being described so many times in the books. (1.she learns that her husband was executed for attempting to kill her and doesn`t even bother to verify it, though the improbability of it is discovered by another character in a minute. 2. a person goes out of the way to help settle her life and she never questions his intentions.)<br />Also it is a little disappointing that inspite of all the plotting and dreaming, we never really see an actual confrontation between the two characters Catherine and Demiris, even after she learns the truth and there is no particular climax to their story as such.<br />The most intriguing character though was that of Melina and how she would finally deal with Demiris and and must say the end to that was satisfying.<br />All in all a good read, though considering the author expected much better.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10938072074505977270">...more</a>

This can be read in short chunks of time, which is nice if you only have a few minutes at a time to read. I don't know if I would bother to read another of his books, unless I was really bored. <div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1087303947">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1087303947" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/17756577-parva-chhanu-chhantyal" class="left imgcol" title="Parva 'chhanu' Chhantyal"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1412016641p2/17756577.jpg" alt="Parva 'chhanu' Chhantyal" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1087303947?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 07, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/17756577-parva-chhanu-chhantyal" class="user" title="Parva 'chhanu' Chhantyal">Parva 'chhanu' Chhantyal</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/17756577-parva-chhanu-chhantyal?shelf=sidney-sheldon" class="actionLinkLite">sidney-sheldon</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/17756577-parva-chhanu-chhantyal?shelf=2014" class="actionLinkLite">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1087303947">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11854877981117182536">Very disappointing that book was!<br /><br />A typical Sidney Sheldon book about love, revenge and jealousy but I hate to say this book didn't live up to my expectation and author's reputation. More than anything, I definitely didn’t like the ending at all. <br /><br />It starts off interestingly with a girl who has a mysterious past. I thought Sidney did it again. The interesting thing about this book is, you have to read it till the end to know how bad it is. I was completely glued to this book just to be disappointe</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11854877981117182536">Very disappointing that book was!<br /><br />A typical Sidney Sheldon book about love, revenge and jealousy but I hate to say this book didn't live up to my expectation and author's reputation. More than anything, I definitely didn’t like the ending at all. <br /><br />It starts off interestingly with a girl who has a mysterious past. I thought Sidney did it again. The interesting thing about this book is, you have to read it till the end to know how bad it is. I was completely glued to this book just to be disappointed at the end. <br /><br />Constantin Demiris (known as Costa) is eager to get a revenge on Catherine (our female character) after her ex-husband (Larry) nicked Costa's mistress (Noelle). He had framed both Larry and Noelle for killing Catherine and because of that, they were executed. Now he is determined to kill Catherine but before that, he wants to do the same thing to her that Larry did to Noelle but in revenge way. Then he starts treating Catherine like a princess claiming to be her ex-husband's boss, and she blindly follows him without any question. And OMG! she is super boring and crying all the time. I have read almost all of Sidney's books but never found a woman like her. All of the sudden he decided to make the woman the weakest character. <br /><br />Finally Catherine finds out that Costa is behind all her trouble and he is the one who killed her husband. I thought then bang!! Now something interesting is going to happen. Now she will do something. Now she will be real Sidney's heroine that we have always known but NO!!! Nothing happened there. They didn’t even encounter and the climax of the story is something surprising but in disappointing way. <br /><br />But this is Sidney Sheldon. It’s his writing. He can make black white and white black. He has that magic to glue his readers to his books. So, I was there reading anxiously that something good will come up. The one thing that kept me reading was I wanted to find out what Melina Lambrou (Costa's wife) was going to do to her husband, after everything he put her through. What she did was expected and clever but her stupid brother ruined it. What I don’t understand is how come Sypros Lambrou saves Costa from going to jail after knowing that he is the main reason for his beloved sister's death. Obviously there is wealth involved and Sypros got greedy. This was totally displeasing. Why Sidney?? Why Why Why?? My heart goes out to Melina. I am probably reading too much of Sidney's book. I guess I need a break!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11854877981117182536">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1860034991424948234">My least favorite protagonist, Catherine Alexander, was back! And still WITHOUT a vengeance! She remained as confused, as befuddled, as weak as ever!<br /><br />Please enlighten me how someone who was supposed to be an avid reader and intelligent wouldn't suspect when her husband and his mistress were executed for "attempting" to murder her.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText1860034991424948234">My least favorite protagonist, Catherine Alexander, was back! And still WITHOUT a vengeance! She remained as confused, as befuddled, as weak as ever!<br /><br />Please enlighten me how someone who was supposed to be an avid reader and intelligent wouldn't suspect when her husband and his mistress were executed for "attempting" to murder her. This kind of mental inadequacy only runs among the less intellectual people. This book was not one of Sidney Sheldon's best as he always epitomized the most cunning and brilliant women as his heroines.<br /><br />Catherine surely fell short with other heroines like Tracy Whitney (If Tomorrow Comes), Jennifer (Rage of Angels), etc. I surely do not take it well when an idiot is portrayed as the leading character, it just doesn't make sense for them to be the center of a book. They should be just one of the background minor characters.<br /><br />Also, Constantin Demiris was NOT impressive at all. He was portrayed almost like an avenging angel to those who were wicked, also to be just as grateful to those who helped him. But I do not think he was grateful at all for there were those who helped/aided him that he murdered: co-pilot whose only mistake was to be the messenger of truth and Chotas for aiding him in accomplishing his wicked plot, they got what they didn't deserve: death from the hands for the one they helped, from Constantin Demiris.<br /><br />Well, sadly this book was centered around Catherine and Demiris which I think were the least interesting characters in its prequel, The Other Side of Midnight. This book shouldn't have been written as it ruined the brilliance of its predecessor. Such an anticlimactic sequel.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1860034991424948234">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1050917421">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1050917421" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/33925226-sheetal-dash" class="left imgcol" title="Sheetal Dash"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1431091826p2/33925226.jpg" alt="Sheetal Dash" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1050917421?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 01, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/33925226-sheetal-dash" class="user" title="Sheetal Dash">Sheetal Dash</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1050917421">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5940900411139993824">Avid fans of Sidney Sheldon will probably enjoy this book. It is indeed as is noted in the editorial reviews a rough-hewn and crudely carved sequel of "The Other Side of Midnight." Sheldon does not deviate from the routine trashy forumla replete with cliche bedroom scenes and a plethora of ruthless characters.<br /><br />Set in the late 1940s right after WWII, Catherine, wife of pilot Larry whom readers first encountered in "The Other Side of Midnight" regains her memory. She remembers how cruel Larry was t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5940900411139993824">Avid fans of Sidney Sheldon will probably enjoy this book. It is indeed as is noted in the editorial reviews a rough-hewn and crudely carved sequel of "The Other Side of Midnight." Sheldon does not deviate from the routine trashy forumla replete with cliche bedroom scenes and a plethora of ruthless characters.<br /><br />Set in the late 1940s right after WWII, Catherine, wife of pilot Larry whom readers first encountered in "The Other Side of Midnight" regains her memory. She remembers how cruel Larry was to her and how he jilted her for his mistress, Noelle Page. Indeed, Noelle was the kept mistress of one Constantin Demiris who was written to sound like an ersatz Ari Onasis. Demiris, like a magician can make those in his disfavor disappear. Exit Larry and Noelle in the first installment.<br /><br />In this book, Catherine, the long-lost heroine is restored to glory and is swept off her feet by a man who is loosely based on the cliche Cavalry men.<br /><br />A psychiatrist and an eclectic mix of patients are thrown into this story; just how they are directly tied into the main plot has never been addressed. One character who is clearly written as an autistic savant displays some of the more prominent autistic behaviors. He is echolalic; he recites long chains of information and he knows the number and type of vehicles he passes in route to the doctor's office. His activities are solitary and few; he does not voluntarily interact with others. I am really tired of stories like this that portray characters with autism as automaton-like savants with isolated abilities that are far removed from the social world. I think stories like this do a grave disservice to those with autism and for others who come across autistic characters because it is just perpetuating a stereotype.<br /><br />This book does not really contain much of a mystery. It's just ruthless people getting even with each other. Even good old Demiris' wife Melina enters this story after having been relegated to shadow figure status in the original. Same old fare.<br /><br />An attorney who was directly involved in a trial engineered by Demiris re-enters the picture. Some fancy manuevering, and he runs away with the show. Literally.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5940900411139993824">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7911541541679408459">Este libro esta promocionado como "la gran secuela esperada", cuando ha sido bueno, pero no lo que yo esperaba, y es que el primer libro me ha encantado, justamente no recuerdo del todo por qué lo ha hecho, pero sí que lo hizo. Estaba algo confundido porque leí la precuela en la secundaria, y no recordaba mucho sobre la historia, sólo tenía en mente mi personaje femenino favorito, el cual por cierto no se trataba de la protagonista, sino de uno secundario, y me he descilucionado un poco porque a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7911541541679408459">Este libro esta promocionado como "la gran secuela esperada", cuando ha sido bueno, pero no lo que yo esperaba, y es que el primer libro me ha encantado, justamente no recuerdo del todo por qué lo ha hecho, pero sí que lo hizo. Estaba algo confundido porque leí la precuela en la secundaria, y no recordaba mucho sobre la historia, sólo tenía en mente mi personaje femenino favorito, el cual por cierto no se trataba de la protagonista, sino de uno secundario, y me he descilucionado un poco porque además pues no está en este libro, lo cual debería haber tenido muy presente, conforme a los hechos jajaja. <br /><br />El libro es entretenido, lo he leído en inglés lo que complico aún más que recordará como habían quedado los hechos, por cierto la protagonista sufre de perdida de memoria, entonces, eran ella y yo recordando las situaciones... Me es curioso como siempre existe un personaje femenino que lo da todo por su ideal, pero que no es el protagónico, pero es el que me termina llamando la atención, Sheldon lo hizo de nuevo, en una medida menor; pero me ha enganchado. </span>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/9068.Sidney_Sheldon">About Sidney Sheldon</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/9068.Sidney_Sheldon"><img alt="9068" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1209169297p2/9068.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer9200594671166075439">Was an American writer who won awards in three careers—a Broadway playwright, a Hollywood TV and movie screenwriter, and a best-selling novelist. His TV works spanned a 20-year period during which he created I Dream of Jeannie (1965-70), Hart to Hart (1979-84), and The Patty Duke Show (1963-66), but it was not until after he turned 50 and began writing best-selling novels such as Master of the Gam</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9200594671166075439">Was an American writer who won awards in three careers—a Broadway playwright, a Hollywood TV and movie screenwriter, and a best-selling novelist. His TV works spanned a 20-year period during which he created I Dream of Jeannie (1965-70), Hart to Hart (1979-84), and The Patty Duke Show (1963-66), but it was not until after he turned 50 and began writing best-selling novels such as Master of the Game (1982), The Other Side of Midnight (1973) and Rage of Angels (1980) that he became most famous.</span>
